## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / dynamical concentration models)
**Analysis**: The target is dA_dt, the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by kinetic rate laws. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are differential rate laws where the reaction rate depends on concentration (reaction order, saturation, autocatalysis) and possibly explicit time-dependence through changing conditions or forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., surface-limited with excess reactant)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, or pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward steady concentration c1)
- Second-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or A + A -> products)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global reaction order c1)
- Mixed-order (polynomial) kinetics: dA_dt = -(c0 * A + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A**3) (parallel pathways with different orders)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating with limiting term: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with depletion/limitation; sigmoidal time course)
- Inhibited/saturated consumption (hyperbolic): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to limited catalyst/active sites)
- Substrate-inhibited form (rate decreases at high A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (high-A inhibition or crowding effects)
- Time-varying pseudo-first-order (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (changing conditions causing rate coefficient to drift in time)
- Time-varying pseudo-first-order (exponential change): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (temperature/programmed ramp or catalyst activation/deactivation modeled in k(t))
- Periodic forcing of rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * A (externally driven kinetics; illumination/flow modulation)
- Nonlinear relaxation to steady state: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) * Abs(A - c1) (quadratic dissipation toward equilibrium; stronger restoring at large deviation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A, it suggests pseudo-first-order/unimolecular kinetics; ln(A) vs t tends to be linear in the noiseless case.
- If dA_dt scales like A**2 (or higher powers), it indicates multi-particle encounters or chain-termination-type behavior; faster decay at higher A.
- A nonzero dA_dt at A ≈ 0 (i.e., intercept) implies zero-order input/consumption, consistent with surface-limited rates or constant feed/bleed terms.
- A stable fixed point A = c1 implied by a factor (A - c1) indicates approach to an equilibrium/steady concentration rather than complete depletion.
- A*(c1 - A) structure implies self-amplification at low A but saturation/depletion at high A, producing sigmoidal concentration trajectories.
- Rational forms like A/(A+c1) imply saturation due to limited catalytic/transport capacity; the effective order transitions from ~1 at low A to ~0 at high A.
- Rational forms with +c2*A**2 in the denominator imply substrate inhibition/crowding where increasing A eventually reduces the effective rate.
- Explicit t-dependence multiplying A (e.g., (c0+c1*t)*A or exp(c*t)*A) suggests changing external conditions (temperature program, catalyst aging, illumination) rather than intrinsic kinetics alone.
- Sin(c*t) or other periodic functions in t indicate driven/forced kinetics, consistent with oscillatory boundary conditions or periodic reactor operation.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK24)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A**c2 + c3*_f*A**c4
Candidate formulas: 76

GT is a fixed function of **A only** (no true dependence on *t*):
\[
0.6338994126\,A^{1/3}\;-\;0.2013223514\,A^{1/2}\;-\;0.2013223514\,A^{2}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be expressible (after choosing its constants) as a linear combination of exactly the three power-laws \(A^{1/3}, A^{1/2}, A^2\) with those coefficients, and must not introduce logs/sin/exp/rational denominators unless they can be eliminated to yield those pure powers.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether its functional form can reduce to those three monomials.

---

### 1
Rational form with denominator \((A+c1)\) and log terms. You can zero out log terms by setting their coefficients to 0, but remaining terms are \(\frac{A^2 c0 + A c2 + A c3}{A+c1}\), a rational function, not a sum of pure powers \(A^{1/3},A^{1/2},A^2\). No way to get fractional powers. **No.**

### 2
All terms divided by \((A+c1)\) and logs. Can kill logs, leaving \(A c0/(A+c1)\), still rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 3
Polynomial in A (up to \(A^3\)), plus rational-in-A pieces, plus a \(t\)-dependent power term. To match GT (no \(t\)), must set \(c6=0\). Then you still only have integer powers and rational terms; cannot produce \(A^{1/3}\) or \(\sqrt A\). **No.**

### 4
Same issue as (3); sin(A⋯) can be removed by \(c6=0\). Still no fractional powers. **No.**

### 5
Has logs (not divided consistently) and a rational \(A/(A+c1)\). Even if logs are removed, remaining is rational/constant, no fractional powers. **No.**

### 6
Has \(t\)-dependent sine; set \(c6=0\). Remaining integer-power polynomial + rational; no fractional powers. **No.**

### 7
Has \(A\exp(c7 t)\); to remove \(t\) dependence set \(c6=0\) (or \(c7=0\) makes it \(A\) times constant, still wrong). Remaining integer powers + rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 8
Has \(\exp(c7 t)\); remove with \(c6=0\). Remaining integer powers + rational. **No.**

### 9
Has \(A(c7+t)^{c8}\); remove with \(c6=0\). Remaining integer powers + rational. **No.**

### 10
Has linear \(t\) term; must set \(c7=0\). Remaining integer powers + rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 11
Has \(t/(A c5+c6)\); must set \(c4=0\). Remaining integer powers + rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 12
All terms over \((A+c1)\) with logs. Kill logs → rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 13
Contains \(A c2\) plus rational/log-over-(A+c1). Kill logs → \(A c0/(A+c1)+A c2\), still not fractional powers and includes rational term unless \(c0=0\). Then just linear \(A\), not GT. **No.**

### 14
All terms are \(\text{polynomial}(A)/(A c1+c2)\): a rational function with only integer powers. Cannot equal a sum of fractional powers on any interval (except trivial single points). **No.**

### 15
Same as (14). **No.**

### 16
Integer-power polynomial plus rational \(A c4/(A c5+c6)\). No fractional powers. **No.**

### 17
Integer-power polynomial plus rational terms. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 18
Integer-power polynomial plus rational terms. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 19
Integer-power polynomial plus linear \(A c6\) and rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 20
Integer-power polynomial plus rational constant term. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 21
Integer-power polynomial plus constant. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 22
Only integer powers and rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 23
Integer-power polynomial plus rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 24
Sum of rational pieces with \((A+c1)\), plus another rational \(A c2/(A+c3)\), plus logs. Kill logs → still rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

### 25
Integer-power polynomial plus \(\frac{A}{A c3+c4}+\frac{c5}{A c3+c4}\) (rational). No fractional powers. **No.**

### 26
\[
\frac{A^{7/3}c0 + A^{4/3}c2 + A^{1/3}c3 + A^2 c4 + A c5}{A^{1/3}+c1}.
\]
Let \(x=A^{1/3}\) (for \(A\ge 0\)). Then expression is \(\frac{c0 x^7 + c2 x^4 + c3 x + c4 x^6 + c5 x^3}{x+c1}\), a rational function in \(x\). If set \(c1=0\), it becomes a polynomial in \(x\): \(c0 x^6 + c4 x^5 + c2 x^3 + c5 x^2 + c3\), i.e. in A: \(c0 A^2 + c4 A^{5/3} + c2 A + c5 A^{2/3} + c3\). This can produce \(A^2\) but **cannot produce** \(A^{1/2}\) (which is \(x^{3/2}\)) and cannot isolate exactly \(A^{1/3}\) without also having incompatible powers unless most coefficients are zero; but then you still can’t get \(\sqrt A\). **No.**

### 27
Rational over \((A+c1)\) plus a \(\log(A c7+c8)\) term over \((A+c1)\). Logs cannot become pure powers for all A. **No.**

### 28
Integer-power polynomial + rational + \(c6\log(c7 t+1)\). To remove \(t\), set \(c6=0\). Still no fractional powers. **No.**

### 29
Same: remove \(t\)-log term by \(c7=0\) or coefficient 0; remaining integer/rational. No fractional powers. **No.**

I need to determine which candidates can match the GT expression:

**GT:** `0.63389941261361888*A**0.333333333333333 - 0.20132235137074334*sqrt(A) - 0.20132235137074334*A**2`

This is: `c_a * A^(1/3) - c_b * A^(1/2) - c_c * A^2`

The key basis functions are: **A^(1/3)**, **A^(1/2)**, and **A^2**. The GT has no dependence on `t`.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. I'll focus on whether each candidate's functional form can produce exactly these three basis functions.

**Key observations:**
- GT uses fractional powers: A^(1/3) and A^(1/2)
- GT has no `t` dependence
- Most candidates use polynomials, rational functions, logarithms, exponentials, or trigonometric functions of A
- Polynomials and rational functions of A cannot produce A^(1/3) or A^(1/2)
- log and exp functions cannot produce fractional powers either

Let me quickly categorize:

**Candidates with log terms:** Candidates 1, 2, 5, 12, 13, 24, 27, 30, 31, 33, 44, 45, 46, 47, 48, 51, 53, 54, 56, 58, 59, 60, 61, 65, 66, 68, 70, 71, 72, 73, 76 — log functions cannot produce fractional powers. **NO MATCH**
